SQL and parameters are ALWAYS kept separate throughout the execution chain\\n2. The database driver's native parameter binding (not Django string interpolation) is used\\n3. RawSQL Expression Sanitization\\n\\nThe `RawSQL` class in `django/db/models/expressions.py` (lines 1236-1268) represents raw SQL expressions used within query annotations. It stores both the SQL template and parameters separately:\\n- Constructor (line 1239) accepts `sql`, `params`, and optional `output_field`\\n- The `as_sql()` method (lines 1248-1249) returns the SQL wrapped in parentheses along with the params tuple: `return \\\"(%s)\\\" % self.sql, self.params`\\n- Parameters are never interpolated into the SQL string directly; they remain separate for database driver parameterization\\n- The `resolve_expression()` method (lines 1254-1268) handles field resolution for parent class fields referenced in raw SQL\\n\\n## 2. raw() QuerySet Method Parameter Binding\\n\\nThe `raw()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1461-1473) creates a `RawQuerySet` instance that handles raw SQL queries returning model instances:\\n- Accepts `raw_query`, `params=()`, `translations=None`, and `using=None`\\n- Creates a `RawQuerySet` object that stores both the SQL query and parameters separately\\n- The `RawQuerySet` class (lines 2210-2237) initializes with the raw query and params, creating an internal `RawQuery` object (line 2231): `self.query = query or sql.RawQuery(sql=raw_query, using=self.db, params=params)`\\n\\n## 3. extra() QuerySet Method for SQL Fragments\\n\\nThe `extra()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1876-1891) allows developers to add raw SQL fragments while maintaining parameter safety:\\n- Accepts `select`, `where`, `params`, `tables`, `order_by`, and `select_params` arguments\\n- Delegates to `clone.query.add_extra()` which maintains separate parameter lists for different SQL fragments\\n- The `params` argument ensures WHERE clause parameters are properly bound\\n- The `select_params` argument ensures SELECT clause parameters are properly bound\\n- Both `where` and `select` fragments use `%s` placeholders that are filled via parameter binding, not string interpolation\\n\\n## 4. cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe core parameter binding enforcement happens through several interconnected components:\\n\\n**RawQuery Execution (django/db/models/sql/query.py, lines 150-220)**:\\n- The `RawQuery._execute_query()` method (lines 203-220) handles the actual execution\\n- It adapts parameters using `connection.ops.adapt_unknown_value()` (lines 209-217) to convert Python types to database-safe values\\n- Type handling for tuple and dict parameters ensures proper escaping based on parameter type (lines 210-217)\\n- The method calls `self.cursor.execute(self.sql, params)` (line 220) with SQL and params separate\\n\\n**CursorWrapper Parameter Handling (django/db/backends/utils.py, lines 17-150)**:\\n- The `CursorWrapper.execute()` method (lines 78-81) delegates to `_execute_with_wrappers()` which passes params separately\\n- The `_execute_with_wrappers()` method (lines 88-92) allows execution wrappers to intercept calls while preserving parameter separation\\n- The `_execute()` method (lines 94-105) validates database state with `validate_no_broken_transaction()` (line 99) and passes params to the actual cursor\\n- If params is None, it calls cursor.execute(sql) without params; otherwise, calls cursor.execute(sql, params) (lines 101-105)\\n- This enforces that parameters are always passed via the database driver's parameter binding mechanism\\n\\n**Parameter Adaptation (django/db/backends/base/operations.py, lines 550-600)**:\\n- The `adapt_unknown_value()` method (lines 550-567) provides type conversion for raw SQL query parameters\\n- Handles datetime, date, time, and decimal conversions before passing to the database (lines 558-567)\\n- These conversions ensure proper escaping while maintaining type safety\\n\\n**Backend-Specific Parameter Handling**:\\n- Each database backend (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle, SQLite) has specific cursor classes that handle parameter conversion\\n- For example, PostgreSQL's `mogrify()` function in `django/db/backends/postgresql/operations.py` (line 195) converts parameters for debugging\\n- Oracle's `_param_generator()` method in `django/db/backends/oracle/base.py` handles Oracle-specific parameter binding\\n\\n**Field-Level Parameter Preparation (django/db/models/fields/__init__.py)**:\\n- Methods like `get_db_prep_value()` and `get_db_prep_save()` ensure field values are properly prepared for database operations\\n- These are called during expression compilation to handle parameter values in ORM queries\\n- While not directly in raw SQL paths, they establish the pattern for parameter preparation\\n\\n**Documentation and Security Enforcement (docs/topics/)**:\\n- `docs/topics/db/sql.txt` (lines 29-35, 262-267) emphasizes that placeholders must NOT be quoted and params must be used\\n- `docs/topics/security.txt` (lines 91-112) defines SQL injection protection strategy and warns about raw SQL methods\\n- `docs/ref/models/expressions.txt` (lines 802-828) documents RawSQL parameters requirement\\n\\n**Security Key Points**:\\n1. SQL and parameters are ALWAYS kept separate throughout the execution chain\\n2. The database driver's native parameter binding (not Django string interpolation) is used\\n3. Parameters are adapted for each backend type using backend-specific methods in `adapt_unknown_value()`\\n4. Unquoted placeholders (`%s`, not `'%s'`) must be used to prevent SQL injection\\n5. The `validate_no_broken_transaction()` call in `_execute()` ensures transaction integrity during parameter binding\\n6. Both `raw()` and `extra()` methods support `params` arguments for safe parameter binding\\n7. When parameters are not provided via params argument, they are adapted from their Python types\\n\\nThis four-layer approach (RawSQL expressions, raw() method, extra() method, and cursor.execute() enforcement) prevents SQL injection by ensuring parameters are never directly interpolated into SQL strings and are instead handled by the database driver's parameterization mechanism, which safely escapes all user input.\""},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":"tool_use","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":78845,"cache_read_input_tokens":30955,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":78845},"output_tokens":2757,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"859b8303-70a9-40ba-9bc5-cc8a97d2fa16","uuid":"352cb715-606a-4ad5-9f61-000000000001"}

RawSQL Expression Sanitization\\n\\nThe `RawSQL` class in `django/db/models/expressions.py` (lines 1236-1268) represents raw SQL expressions used within query annotations. It stores both the SQL template and parameters separately:\\n- Constructor (line 1239) accepts `sql`, `params`, and optional `output_field`\\n- The `as_sql()` method (lines 1248-1249) returns the SQL wrapped in parentheses along with the params tuple: `return \\\"(%s)\\\" % self.sql, self.params`\\n- Parameters are never interpolated into the SQL string directly; they remain separate for database driver parameterization\\n- The `resolve_expression()` method (lines 1254-1268) handles field resolution for parent class fields referenced in raw SQL\\n\\n## 2. raw() QuerySet Method Parameter Binding\\n\\nThe `raw()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1461-1473) creates a `RawQuerySet` instance that handles raw SQL queries returning model instances:\\n- Accepts `raw_query`, `params=()`, `translations=None`, and `using=None`\\n- Creates a `RawQuerySet` object that stores both the SQL query and parameters separately\\n- The `RawQuerySet` class (lines 2210-2237) initializes with the raw query and params, creating an internal `RawQuery` object (line 2231): `self.query = query or sql.RawQuery(sql=raw_query, using=self.db, params=params)`\\n\\n## 3. extra() QuerySet Method for SQL Fragments\\n\\nThe `extra()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1876-1891) allows developers to add raw SQL fragments while maintaining parameter safety:\\n- Accepts `select`, `where`, `params`, `tables`, `order_by`, and `select_params` arguments\\n- Delegates to `clone.query.add_extra()` which maintains separate parameter lists for different SQL fragments\\n- The `params` argument ensures WHERE clause parameters are properly bound\\n- The `select_params` argument ensures SELECT clause parameters are properly bound\\n- Both `where` and `select` fragments use `%s` placeholders that are filled via parameter binding, not string interpolation\\n\\n## 4. cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe core parameter binding enforcement happens through several interconnected components:\\n\\n**RawQuery Execution (django/db/models/sql/query.py, lines 150-220)**:\\n- The `RawQuery._execute_query()` method (lines 203-220) handles the actual execution\\n- It adapts parameters using `connection.ops.adapt_unknown_value()` (lines 209-217) to convert Python types to database-safe values\\n- Type handling for tuple and dict parameters ensures proper escaping based on parameter type (lines 210-217)\\n- The method calls `self.cursor.execute(self.sql, params)` (line 220) with SQL and params separate\\n\\n**CursorWrapper Parameter Handling (django/db/backends/utils.py, lines 17-150)**:\\n- The `CursorWrapper.execute()` method (lines 78-81) delegates to `_execute_with_wrappers()` which passes params separately\\n- The `_execute_with_wrappers()` method (lines 88-92) allows execution wrappers to intercept calls while preserving parameter separation\\n- The `_execute()` method (lines 94-105) validates database state with `validate_no_broken_transaction()` (line 99) and passes params to the actual cursor\\n- If params is None, it calls cursor.execute(sql) without params; otherwise, calls cursor.execute(sql, params) (lines 101-105)\\n- This enforces that parameters are always passed via the database driver's parameter binding mechanism\\n\\n**Parameter Adaptation (django/db/backends/base/operations.py, lines 550-600)**:\\n- The `adapt_unknown_value()` method (lines 550-567) provides type conversion for raw SQL query parameters\\n- Handles datetime, date, time, and decimal conversions before passing to the database (lines 558-567)\\n- These conversions ensure proper escaping while maintaining type safety\\n\\n**Backend-Specific Parameter Handling**:\\n- Each database backend (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle, SQLite) has specific cursor classes that handle parameter conversion\\n- For example, PostgreSQL's `mogrify()` function in `django/db/backends/postgresql/operations.py` (line 195) converts parameters for debugging\\n- Oracle's `_param_generator()` method in `django/db/backends/oracle/base.py` handles Oracle-specific parameter binding\\n\\n**Field-Level Parameter Preparation (django/db/models/fields/__init__.py)**:\\n- Methods like `get_db_prep_value()` and `get_db_prep_save()` ensure field values are properly prepared for database operations\\n- These are called during expression compilation to handle parameter values in ORM queries\\n- While not directly in raw SQL paths, they establish the pattern for parameter preparation\\n\\n**Documentation and Security defines SQL injection protection strategy and warns about raw SQL methods\\n- `docs/ref/models/expressions.txt` (lines 802-828) documents RawSQL parameters requirement\\n\\n**Security Key with the raw query and params, creating an internal `RawQuery` object (line 2231): `self.query = query or sql.RawQuery(sql=raw_query, using=self.db, params=params)`\\n\\n## 3. extra() QuerySet Method for SQL Fragments\\n\\nThe `extra()` method in `django/db/models/query.py` (lines 1876-1891) allows developers to add raw SQL fragments while maintaining parameter safety:\\n- Accepts `select`, `where`, `params`, `tables`, `order_by`, and `select_params` arguments\\n- Delegates to `clone.query.add_extra()` which maintains separate parameter lists for different SQL fragments\\n- The `params` argument ensures WHERE clause parameters are properly bound\\n- The `select_params` argument ensures SELECT clause parameters are properly bound\\n- Both `where` and `select` fragments use `%s` placeholders that are filled via parameter binding, not string interpolation\\n\\n## 4. cursor.execute() Parameterization Enforcement\\n\\nThe core parameter binding enforcement happens through several interconnected components:\\n\\n**RawQuery Execution (django/db/models/sql/query.py, lines 150-220)**:\\n- The `RawQuery._execute_query()` method (lines 203-220) handles the actual proper escaping based on parameter type (lines 210-217)\\n- The method calls `self.cursor.execute(self.sql, params)` (line 220) with SQL and params separate\\n\\n**CursorWrapper Parameter Handling with `validate_no_broken_transaction()` (line 99) and passes params to the actual cursor\\n- If params is None, it calls cursor.execute(sql) without params; otherwise, calls cursor.execute(sql, params) (lines 101-105)\\n- This enforces that parameters are always passed via the database driver's parameter binding mechanism\\n\\n**Parameter Adaptation (django/db/backends/base/operations.py, to the database (lines 558-567)\\n- These conversions ensure proper escaping while maintaining type safety\\n\\n**Backend-Specific Parameter Handling**:\\n- Each database backend (MySQL, PostgreSQL, parameters for debugging\\n- Oracle's `_param_generator()` method in `django/db/backends/oracle/base.py` handles Oracle-specific parameter binding\\n\\n**Field-Level Parameter Preparation (django/db/models/fields/__init__.py)**:\\n- Methods like `get_db_prep_value()` and `get_db_prep_save()` ensure field values are properly prepared for database operations\\n- These are called during expression compilation to handle parameter values in ORM queries\\n- While not directly in raw SQL paths, they establish the pattern for parameter preparation\\n\\n**Documentation and Security Enforcement (docs/topics/)**:\\n- `docs/topics/db/sql.txt` (lines 29-35, 262-267) emphasizes that placeholders must NOT be quoted and params must be used\\n- `docs/topics/security.txt` (lines 91-112) Points**:\\n1.
